    <div class="content">
     <article class="article-container article--post">
      <header class="article__header">
       <div class="article__title-wrapper">
        <h1 class="article__title">
         X is launching two new subscription tiers, including a ‘Premium+’ ad-free plan
        </h1>
       </div>
       <div class="article__byline-wrapper">
        <div class="article__byline">
         <a href="https://techcrunch.com/author/aisha-malik/">
          Aisha Malik
         </a>
         <span class="article__byline__meta">
          1 week
         </span>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="article__featured-image-wrapper breakout">
        <img class="article__featured-image" src="https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2023/08/twitter-x-logo-musk-2.jpg?w=711"/>
       </div>
      </header>
      <div class="article-content">
       <p id="speakable-summary">
        X, formerly known as Twitter, is introducing
        <a href="https://twitter.com/premium/status/1717977644996644948" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
         two new tiers
        </a>
        for its subscription offering in order to bring in additional revenue. The social media giant is adding a new Premium+ tier that costs $16 per month and offers the “largest reply boost” and removes ads from the For You and Following feeds. The tier also comes with revenue-sharing, along with access to other creator tools.
       </p>
       <p>
        The second tier launching today is called “Basic” and costs $3 per month. The tier doesn’t come with a blue checkmark, but includes basic features like the ability to edit posts and post longer text and videos. It also offers a “small reply boost.”
       </p>
       <div class="embed breakout embed-oembed embed--twitter">
        <blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-dnt="true" data-width="550">
         <p dir="ltr" lang="en">
          introducing Premium+
         </p>
         <p>
          – no ads in For You or Following
          <br/>
          – largest boost for your replies (vs other Premium tiers or unverified users)
          <br/>
          – access to our full suite of creator tools
         </p>
         <p>
          now available on Web ✌️
         </p>
         <p>
          subscribe here →
          <a href="https://t.co/Ywvyijo9CQ">
           https://t.co/Ywvyijo9CQ
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          — Premium (@premium)
          <a href="https://twitter.com/premium/status/1717977644996644948?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">
           October 27, 2023
          </a>
         </p>
        </blockquote>
        <div class="piano-inline-promo">
        </div>
        <p>
        </p>
       </div>
       <p>
        Both of the new tiers are now available on the web.
       </p>
       <p>
        The new tiers join the standard X Premium tier, which replaced Twitter Blue. The tier costs $8 per month and gives users a blue checkmark, prioritized ranking in replies, bookmark folders, longer posts, text formatting, themes, sms two-factor authentication, encrypted DMs and more.
       </p>
       <p>
        The launch of the new tiers comes
        <a href="https://techcrunch.com/2023/10/06/x-to-test-three-tiers-of-its-premium-service-ceo-says-code-shows-one-tier-may-be-ad-free/">
         a few weeks
        </a>
        after
        <a href="https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2023-10-05/x-tells-bankers-that-advertisers-are-back-but-spending-less?sref=gni836kR" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
         Bloomberg
        </a>
        reported that X was working on new subscription tiers.
       </p>
       <p>
        The introduction of the new tiers will give X additional ways to grow revenues as it deals with the loss in advertising dollars that it has faced since Elon Musk took the reins of the platform last fall. Musk’s controversial changes have turned away advertisers, as major companies ended up pulling their ads from the social network after their ads were displayed next to hate speech
        <a data-mrf-link="https://fortune.com/2023/08/17/twitter-x-ads-pro-nazi-account-right-wing-hate-groups/" href="https://fortune.com/2023/08/17/twitter-x-ads-pro-nazi-account-right-wing-hate-groups/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
         and pro-Nazi content.
        </a>
        Earlier this month,
        <a data-mrf-link="https://www.reuters.com/technology/us-ad-revenue-musks-x-declined-each-month-since-takeover-data-2023-10-04/" href="https://www.reuters.com/technology/us-ad-revenue-musks-x-declined-each-month-since-takeover-data-2023-10-04/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
         Reuters
        </a>
        reported that the company’s U.S. ad revenue has declined every month since Musk took over, with the latest figures showing a 60% year-over-year decline as of August.
       </p>
       <p>
        Since taking over the company last year, Musk has been looking for ways to generate additional revenue, and has gone so far as charging users in New Zealand and the Philippines
        <a href="https://techcrunch.com/2023/10/17/x-starts-experimenting-with-a-1-per-year-fee-for-new-users">
         $1 per year
        </a>
        in order to access the social network.
       </p>
       <div class="embed breakout embed-oembed embed--techcrunch">
        <blockquote class="wp-embedded-content" data-secret="w3xp4u7QHX">
         <p>
          <a href="https://techcrunch.com/2023/10/27/a-year-after-musks-takeover-x-says-an-average-user-spends-32-minutes-per-day-on-the-platform/">
           A year after Musk’s takeover, X says an average user spends 32 minutes per day on the platform
          </a>
         </p>
        </blockquote>
        <p>
        </p>
       </div>
      </div>
      <footer class="article-footer">
       <input class="shortlink" readonly="" title="Article Shortlink" type="text" value=""/>
      </footer>
     </article>
    </div>

  <script id="tc-app-js-extra">
   var tc_app_data = {"ads":{"gemini_enabled":false,"gemini_codes":{"position_4":{"mobile":"ae64471c-14c2-4457-8e9b-a5190206eafd","desktop":"b2018d9e-dedc-4e85-8823-b06917beb892"},"position_8":{"mobile":"619392a1-b497-4aa9-b683-24aab7246c16","desktop":"05c0b21d-e742-494d-ac59-474e3feaa4b8"}}},"assetURI":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/themes\/techcrunch-2017","breaking":"0","live_event":"0","livestream":"","feature_islands":{"homepage":[{"id":2623356,"date":"2023-11-04T11:44:18","date_gmt":"2023-11-04T18:44:18","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2623356"},"modified":"2023-11-04T16:57:58","modified_gmt":"2023-11-04T23:57:58","slug":"san-francisco-office-space-2","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/04\/san-francisco-office-space-2\/","title":{"rendered":"A new breed of companies expand in San Francisco&#8217;s prime areas"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">Ten years ago<\/span>, <a href=\"https:\/\/pear.vc\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Pear VC<\/a>, then a tiny new venture firm, operated out of a nondescript office in Palo Alto that was enlivened by bright, computer-themed art. Last week, the outfit \u2014 which closed its <a href=\"ttps:\/\/www.businesswire.com\/news\/home\/20230530005616\/en\/Pear-VC-Closes-an-Oversubscribed-432-Million-Seed-Fund\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">largest fund<\/a> to date in May \u2014 quietly inked a deal to sublease 30,000 square feet of &#8220;Class A&#8221; office space in San Francisco\u2019s Mission Bay neighborhood from the file-storage giant Dropbox.<\/p>\n<p>It\u2019s among a number of fast-growing outfits taking up more space in San Francisco as an earlier generation of companies shrinks its physical footprint.<\/p>\n<p>As the San Francisco Chronicle first <a href=\"https:\/\/www.sfchronicle.com\/realestate\/article\/openai-s-f-uber-lease-18451102.php\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reported<\/a> last week, ChatGPT creator OpenAI just subleased two buildings totaling a collective 486,600 square feet from Uber. The ride-share giant, which originally leased a grouping of four buildings down the street from Dropbox and will continue to occupy two of these, told the paper it is \u201cright-sizing.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>A rival to OpenAI \u2014 Anthropic \u2014 also just reportedly closed a <a href=\"https:\/\/www.sfchronicle.com\/bayarea\/article\/s-f-ai-firm-leasing-entire-former-slack-hq-18341028.php\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">sizable subleasing deal<\/a>. Its plan: to take over the entire 250,000-square-foot building in downtown San Francisco that was previously Slack&#8217;s headquarters.<\/p>\n<p>Salesforce, which acquired Slack in 2021, is an investor in Anthropic. Meanwhile, Pear VC co-founder Pejman Nozad wrote one of the first small checks to Dropbox when he was still relatively new to the U.S. from Iran and selling Persian rugs to Silicon Valley bigwigs.<\/p>\n<p>Such subleases don\u2019t necessarily begin with hand-shake deals, however. Asked if Nozad zeroed in on Pear\u2019s new space owing to his connection to Dropbox, he scoffs. The office &#8212; which has room for more than 200 desks, features more than 20 conference and call rooms, and has dedicated event space to host talks &#8212; \u201cwas a business deal for them,\u201d says Nozad. \u201cThe founders were not involved. As you know, I sold rugs for 17 years, so I have some skills in negotiation,\u201d he adds with a laugh.<\/p>\n<p>Certainly, it&#8217;s a good time to strike a subleasing deal if you&#8217;re a well-funded company on the rise. According to Colin Yasukochi, an executive director at the commercial real estate services firm CBRE, subleases in prime areas like Mission Bay and the city&#8217;s Financial District currently range from $60 to $80 per square foot. The higher the floor and the more plentiful the amenities, the higher the price. For startups willing to sublease space with less than five years left on the lessee&#8217;s contract, the better the terms (as they&#8217;ll need to lease again somewhere else in the not-too-distant future). In comparison, office lease rates passed the $75 per square foot mark in September 2019 before the pandemic turned the city upside down.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>There&#8217;s no shortage of options right now. San Francisco&#8217;s commercial buildings are currently 35% vacant, and there are still more tenants flowing out the door than entering them.<\/p>\n<p>Dropbox originally leased the entire 750,000-square-foot space in the building it currently occupies, but it never filled it up entirely and after COVID struck, it began more aggressively whittling down its use. It paid $32 million in late 2021 to <a href=\"https:\/\/therealdeal.com\/sanfrancisco\/2021\/12\/23\/dropbox-pays-32m-to-terminate-part-of-its-lease-in-its-sf-hq\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">terminate<\/a> part of its 15-year lease; before newly subleasing space to Pear VC, it separately subleased roughly 200,000 square feet to two different life sciences companies: Vir Biotechnology and BridgeBio. It&#8217;s still less than half full.<\/p>\n<p>This week, Adobe listed half its leased footprint in San Francisco\u2019s Showplace Square neighborhood and is now looking to sublease <a href=\"https:\/\/www.bizjournals.com\/sanfrancisco\/news\/2023\/11\/01\/adobe-100-hooper-sublease.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">156,000 square feet<\/a> across three floors of one of the buildings it used to occupy.<\/p>\n<p>But a tipping point is seemingly in sight. There was &#8220;negative net absorption&#8221; of 1.85 million square feet in San Francisco in the third quarter of this year, according to CBRE data; at the same time, market demand reached 5.2 million square feet, which is the highest increase since the first quarter of 2020.<\/p>\n<p>Much of that shift can be traced to companies like OpenAI, suggests Yasukochi, who says that a new spate of outfits is starting to set up shop, enticed by the opportunity to rent sleeker space for the same or better prices than was possible several years ago for less finished locations, and in more central areas of the city. &#8220;It&#8217;s a huge opportunity for companies that are trying to bring back their employees,&#8221; says Yasukochi. (OpenAI CEO Sam Altman has long said he thinks companies are more effective when employees <a href=\"https:\/\/fortune.com\/2023\/05\/05\/openai-ceo-sam-altman-remote-work-mistake-return-to-office\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">convene in person<\/a>.)<\/p>\n<p>Indeed, Yasukochi anticipates that if the economy improves in the second half of next year and interest rates come down, tech outfits in particular will be positioned to recover faster &#8212; and pull the city along with them. &#8220;Many tech companies were quick to cut excess employees, along with real estate and other costs,&#8221; says Yasukochi. He also says that while tech outfits are typically &#8220;early to cut back, they&#8217;re also early to grow. I don&#8217;t see any other industry that generates the volume of growth that tech can.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Worth noting: Yasukochi does not think those tech companies will necessarily be growing in San Francisco&#8217;s Hayes Valley. Though the small shop-studded neighborhood has led a resurgence of interest in San Francisco this year and eagerly embraced the moniker &#8220;Cerebral Valley,&#8221; owing to its concentration of AI communities, most of those teams, he observes, are &#8220;meeting in restaurants and bars and working out of their apartments.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>The reality, Yasukochi continues, is &#8220;there isn&#8217;t a lot of office space there.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><em>Pictured above: 1800 Owens Street in San Francisco, which is the site of Dropbox&#8217;s headquarters and now, Pear VC&#8217;s San Francisco office, too.<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Ten years ago, Pear VC, then a tiny new venture firm, operated out of a nondescript office in Palo Alto that was enlivened by bright, computer-themed art. Last week, the outfit \u2014 which closed its largest fund to date in May \u2014 quietly inked a deal to sublease 30,000 square feet of &#8220;Class A&#8221; office en-source-model","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/05\/valued-at-1b-kai-fu-lees-llm-startup-unveils-open-source-model\/","title":{"rendered":"Valued at $1B, Kai-Fu Lee&#8217;s LLM startup unveils open source model"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">Kai-Fu Lee, the<\/span> computer scientist known in the West for his bestseller <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/06\/07\/dr-kai-fu-lee-is-coming-to-disrupt-sf-to-talk-about-how-ai-will-eat-everything-especially-jobs\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>AI Superpowers<\/em><\/a>\u00a0and in China for his bets on <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/06\/13\/momenta-profile\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">artificial intelligence unicorns<\/a>, has a new venture &#8212; and a great ambition.<\/p>\n<p>In late March, Lee launched a company called<a href=\"https:\/\/01.ai\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> 01.AI<\/a> with the vision to develop a homegrown large language model for the Chinese market. The venture puts him in competition with other prominent Chinese tech leaders, including<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/07\/11\/chinas-search-engine-pioneer-unveils-open-source-large-language-model-to-rival-openai\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">\u00a0Sogou&#8217;s founder Wang Xiaochuan<\/a>, who have been swiftly gathering talent and venture capital to establish China&#8217;s equivalents of OpenAI.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;I think necessity is the mother of innovation, and there&#8217;s clearly a huge necessity in China,&#8221; Lee, who&#8217;s 61 and leading 01.AI as CEO, told TechCrunch in an interview, explaining the motive behind starting the company. &#8220;Unlike the rest of the world, China doesn&#8217;t have access to OpenAI and Google because those two companies did not make their products available in China, so I think many doing LLM are trying to do their part in creating a solution for a market that really needs this.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>01.AI&#8217;s growth is a fitting reflection of the rapid development in the generative AI field. Seven months after its founding, the startup has released its first model, the open-source <a href=\"https:\/\/github.com\/01-ai\/Yi\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Yi-34B<\/a>. The decision to introduce an open LLM as its debut product is a way to &#8220;give back&#8221; to society, said Lee. For people who have felt LLaMA is a &#8220;godsend&#8221; to them, &#8220;we&#8217;ve provided a compelling alternative,&#8221; he added.<\/p>\n<p>As of writing, Yi-34B, which is a bilingual (English and Chinese) base model trained with 34 billion parameters and significantly smaller than other open models like Falcon-180B and Meta LlaMa2-70B, <span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">came in first amongst pre-trained LLM models, <a href=\"https:\/\/huggingface.co\/spaces\/HuggingFaceH4\/open_llm_leaderboard\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according to a ranking by Hugging Face<\/a>.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We still believe that larger models, when trained well, on a large amount of high-quality data, will always outperform substantially smaller models of comparable quality and comparable technology, so I think [Yi-34B] outperforming much larger models is something that we don&#8217;t usually see,&#8221; said Lee. &#8220;We feel quite confident as we released models that are 100 billion to 400 billion over the next coming year, year and a half, these models will be dramatically better than today&#8217;s model that we announced.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>The startup&#8217;s ability to commence model training quickly is no doubt an outcome of its smooth fundraising, which is critical to securing top-tier talent and AI processors. While declining to disclose how much 01.AI has raised, Lee said it&#8217;s valued at $1 billion after receiving financing from Sinovation Ventures, Alibaba Cloud and other undisclosed investors.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>01.AI has already grown to more than 100 employees, over half of whom are LLM experts from major multinational and Chinese tech firms. Its vice president of technology, for instance, is an early member of Google&#8217;s Bard, and its chief architect was a founding member of TensorFlow and worked alongside renowned researchers like Jeff Dean and Samy Bengio at Google Brain. The key figures behind Yi-34B are Wenhao Huang, a Microsoft Research Asia veteran, and Ethan Dai, who held senior AI positions at Huawei and Alibaba.<\/p>\n<p>Having backed over ten unicorns and venture-built seven companies through Sinovation Ventures, Lee is possibly one of the most well-connected investors and entrepreneurs in China.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;It&#8217;s been, you know, over 25 years since the founding of Microsoft Research Asia, and everything I&#8217;ve done has been about getting super great talent,&#8221; said Lee, who launched Microsoft Research Asia, the U.S. giant&#8217;s biggest research center abroad, before spearheading Google China. Over the years, Microsoft Research Asia has earned the reputation as the &#8220;West Point&#8221; for nurturing China&#8217;s AI entrepreneurs.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Now, of course, you want to pay people fairly, and you need to be competitive in pay, but I really think that it&#8217;s also about people believing they can make a difference and believing the company can succeed,&#8221; said Lee, appearing in a video call at 9:30 p.m. Beijing time. His staff were just as self-motivating. One of the startup&#8217;s infrastructure experts was working well into the wee hours that day, still messaging Lee at 2:15 a.m. to express his excitement about being part of 01.AI&#8217;s mission.<\/p>\n<p>It&#8217;s no secret that building LLMs is a costly undertaking. To sustain its cash-intensive operations, 01.AI has plans for monetization right from the start. While the company will continue to open source some of its models, its objective is to build a state-of-the-art proprietary model that serves as a foundation for a diverse range of commercial products.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We<span class=\"notion-enable-hover\" data-token-index=\"0\"> can\u2019t open source everything,&#8221; said Lee. &#8220;We were quite cognizant of the fact that these large language models require a lot of compute, and therefore, are very expensive. When we raise a lot of money, most of it will be spent on the GPU. Given that, we needed to first acquire as much GPU as we could, which we did.&#8221;<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Like other LLM players in China, 01.AI has proactively stockpiled GPUs in anticipation of U.S. sanctions; it borrowed money to buy processors even before it landed funding. Over the past year, the Biden administration has heightened restrictions on China&#8217;s access to high-end AI chips, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/technology\/inside-chinas-underground-market-high-end-nvidia-ai-chips-2023-06-19\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">prompting Chinese firms to pay inflated prices for chips<\/a>. The foresight was rewarded &#8212; 01.AI now has a supply that will suffice for<span class=\"notion-enable-hover\" data-token-index=\"0\"> at least the next 12-18 months.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Aside from causing headaches for Chinese firms, U.S. sanctions have been a catalyst for innovation by encouraging them to optimize the use of computing power. &#8220;With a very high-quality infrastructure team, for every 1000 GPUs, we might be able to squeeze 2000 GPUs workload out of them,&#8221; said Lee.<\/p>\n<p>01.AI&#8217;s path to monetization hinges largely on its ability to find product-market fit for its expensive AI models. While top-notch LLM scientists are scarce, there&#8217;s no shortage of product talent in China.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;China&#8217;s not ahead of the U.S. in LLM, but there&#8217;s no doubt China can build better applications than American developers mostly because of the phenomenal mobile internet ecosystem that was built over the last 12 years or so,&#8221; argued Lee.<\/p>\n<p>While the founder gave no details on the services in the pipeline, he hinted that the company is experimenting with concepts in the productivity and social directions, and he&#8217;d be &#8220;disappointed&#8221; if 01.AI didn&#8217;t release an app within this calendar year.<\/p>\n<p>The startup&#8217;s ultimate goal, according to Lee, is to become an ecosystem where outside developers can build applications easily. &#8220;The duty is not just to push out good research models, but even more importantly to make application development easy so that there can be compelling applications,&#8221; he said. &#8220;At the end of the day. It is an ecosystem play.&#8221; Time will tell if Lee&#8217;s AI endeavor will pay off.<!-- notionvc: 8d4876fe-0354-42b4-ae71-26dead0bd2cc --><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout embed-oembed embed--techcrunch\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Fi91Q4zwzN\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/07\/11\/chinas-search-engine-pioneer-unveils-open-source-large-language-model-to-rival-openai\/\">China&#8217;s search engine pioneer unveils open source large language model to rival OpenAI<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; circular economy promises to remake retail. Why is it so hard to trust?"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">Thrifting is back<\/span>, though this time it has a tech spin on it.<\/p>\n<p>An entirely new generation has discovered the pleasures of digging through other people\u2019s discarded clothes in the hopes of finding the perfect piece. Hoping to cash in on the trend, companies have been embracing resale platforms, allowing them to capture some residual value while polishing their sustainability bona fides.<\/p>\n<p>If it sounds too good to be true, it is for now, at least. Brand-owned resale still has a few kinks to work out if it\u2019s going to transform retail.<\/p>\n<p>Few companies have embraced resale as much as Patagonia, the outdoor gear supplier. Its <a href=\"https:\/\/wornwear.patagonia.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Worn Wear<\/a> program, which began as a used clothing section in its retail stores, is now a full e-commerce site that offers discounts on items with plenty of life in them. For brand aficionados, it also gives them access to back catalog items that are no longer available. It\u2019s been a decade-long experiment that teases what a future circular economy might look like.<\/p>\n<p>For companies like Patagonia, brand-owned resale is appealing for several reasons. The privately held company\u2019s clothing has a reputation for being \u201cbuy it for life,\u201d and its items tend to last for years, even decades. Plus, for a company that has staked its name on sustainability, selling used clothing is a logical extension of the brand.<\/p>\n<p>For other companies, even if sustainability isn\u2019t a key differentiator, brand-owned resale sites can help capture some of the value that would otherwise go to secondhand markets like eBay, Poshmark, Mercari and others.<\/p>\n<p>To fill Worn Wear\u2019s virtual shelves, Patagonia pays people for their old clothing. Not as much as they might get if they were to sell them directly on other resale sites, but it promises to be a simpler process: either drop off the clothes at a Patagonia retail store or mail them in. The company\u2019s partner, <a href=\"https:\/\/trove.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Trove<\/a>, handles the rest.<\/p>\n<p>Once an item arrives at Trove\u2019s warehouse in California, a team of workers inspects and photographs it. It also compares the item ID against a database it maintains to determine whether the piece is authentic. Items that can\u2019t be identified (maybe the item ID is unreadable), the company employs computer vision to narrow the possibilities. The workers log descriptions of each item\u2019s condition so that once they appear on the resale site, which Trove also manages, customers have a decent idea of what they\u2019re buying. Since each item that winds its way through Trove\u2019s warehouse has different wear patterns, they all receive unique SKUs. Partners can monitor their resale platform\u2019s performance through dashboards, reports and CRM integrations.<\/p>\n<p>Trove has ridden the resale wave, raising over $150 million total, including an early-stage investment from Tin Shed Ventures, Patagonia\u2019s venture capital fund. It\u2019s not the only resale platform that works directly with brands, but it\u2019s broadly considered a leader. Recently, though, Trove appears to have stumbled. Its Series E round, which closed in July, added another $30 million to its coffers but also cut its valuation in half, according to PitchBook. Still, the resale company has managed to attract a dozen clothing and outdoor gear companies to its platform, including not just Patagonia but also REI, Levi\u2019s, Lululemon, Allbirds and others.<div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"><\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Even if sustainability isn\u2019t a key differentiator, brand-owned resale sites can help capture some of the value that would otherwise go to secondhand markets.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"author":133574548,"featured_media":2624469,"comment_status":"open","ping_status":"closed","sticky":false,"template":"","format":"standard","meta":{"amp_status":"","relegenceEntities":[],"relegenceSubjects":[],"carmot_uuid":"2e3ec032-2294-30cb-8aa0-e28fc09db74a","footnotes":"","apple_news_api_created_at":"","apple_news_api_id":"","apple_news_api_modified_at":"","apple_news_api_revision":"","apple_news_api_share_url":"","apple_news_coverimage":0,"apple_news_coverimage_caption":"","apple_news_is_hidden":false,"apple_news_is_paid":false,"apple_news_is_preview":false,"apple_news_is_sponsored":false,"apple_news_maturity_rating":"","apple_news_metadata":"\"\"","apple_news_pullquote":"","apple_news_pullquote_position":"","apple_news_slug":"","apple_news_sections":"\"\"","apple_news_suppress_video_url":false,"apple_news_use_image_component":false},"categories":[576957003],"tags":[576858236,3737,1007732,2342086],"crunchbase_tag":[],"tc_stories_tax":[],"tc_ec_category":[576796356],"tc_event":[],"tc_regions_tax":[],"yoast_head":"<!-- This site is optimized with the Yoast SEO Premium plugin v20.2.1 (Yoast SEO v20.2.1) - https:\/\/yoast.com\/wordpress\/plugins\/seo\/ -->\n<title>The circular economy promises to remake retail. new real-time app scanning aims to combat malicious sideloaded apps"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">Android&#8217;s in-built security<\/span> engine Google Play Protect has a new feature that conducts a real-time analysis of an Android app&#8217;s code and blocks it from installing the app if it&#8217;s considered potentially harmful.<\/p>\n<p>Google announced in October <a href=\"https:\/\/security.googleblog.com\/2023\/10\/enhanced-google-play-protect-real-time.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">the new real-time app scanning feature<\/a> built into Google Play Protect that the company says can help catch malicious or fake sideloaded apps installed from outside the app store. These apps will morph their appearance or use AI to alter the apps&#8217; code in a way that helps them avoid detection.<\/p>\n<p>Google said this Play Protect feature now recommends a real-time app scan for any new app that has never been scanned before. This consists of a code analysis that will &#8220;extract important signals from the app and send them to the Play Protect backend infrastructure for a code-level evaluation.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Android&#8217;s app store has billions of apps that Google screens for malware, though <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/05\/29\/popular-android-app-microphone-spying-google-play\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">not always successfully<\/a>. Many device owners also take to sideloading Android apps, which skirt the app store altogether and its many lines of defense. Sideloading remains a popular feature for Android users, even if it means having to trust that the app they are installing is not malicious.<\/p>\n<p>One of the key reasons for Google to introduce its enhanced real-time code-level scanning feature is to counter the proliferation of predatory loan apps. These apps have resulted in the harassment of users, leading in some cases to victims taking their own lives. Bad actors gain access to user data, including contacts and photos, which are used to bully users. TechCrunch <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/08\/26\/loan-apps-abuse-harassment-suicide-indian-users-google-apple-india\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">extensively covered<\/a> the impact of predatory loan apps on Indian users. Google also said it took down over 3,500 such apps in the year for violating its policy requirements. Attackers still find ways to target their victims.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Our policies are making it tougher for predatory apps to be listed on the Play Store. But the bad actors are inventive, and they are finding new ways to trick people and that is why we take additional measures,&#8221; said Saikat Mitra, Google&#8217;s head of trust and safety for APAC at the Google for India event in New Delhi last month, while announcing the update to Play Protect.<\/p>\n<p>Google initially launched the Play Protect update in India, with plans to soon expand internationally. TechCrunch tried the feature out for ourselves by loading a phone with a variety of malicious and bad apps to see what would make it through.<\/p>\n<p>We tried to install more than 30 different malicious apps, from stalkerware and spyware to predatory loan apps and fake ripoffs of popular apps. Google Play Protect blocked nearly all of the malicious apps with warnings like, &#8220;Apps from unknown developers can sometimes be unsafe,&#8221; and &#8220;This app tries to spy on your personal data, such as SMS messages, photos, audio recordings, or call history,&#8221; or, &#8220;This app is fake.&#8221; A handful of recently created predatory loan apps, however, were successfully installed.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2624821\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2624821\" decoding=\"async\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2624821\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/google-pplay-protect-scanning-apps.jpg\" alt=\"three screenshots showing Google Play Protect's real-time app scanning in effect\" width=\"1024\" height=\"532\" data-wp-editing=\"1\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/google-pplay-protect-scanning-apps.jpg 1995w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/google-pplay-protect-scanning-apps.jpg?resize=150,78 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/google-pplay-protect-scanning-apps.jpg?resize=300,156 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/google-pplay-protect-scanning-apps.jpg?resize=768,399 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/google-pplay-protect-scanning-apps.jpg?resize=680,353 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/google-pplay-protect-scanning-apps.jpg?resize=1536,798 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/google-pplay-protect-scanning-apps.jpg?resize=1200,623 1200w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2023\/11\/google-pplay-protect-scanning-apps.jpg?resize=50,26 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2624821\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Screenshots showing Google Play Protect&#8217;s real-time app scanning checking to see if an app is malicious. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> <a href=\"https:\/\/security.googleblog.com\/2023\/10\/enhanced-google-play-protect-real-time.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Google<\/a><\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>To test out the scope of the Play Protect update, we used a Pixel 7a with a fresh install of Android 14 with the updated Google Play Store featuring real-time code-level scanning.<\/p>\n<p>We began the testing on the Pixel 7a by trying to install various spyware apps that have rebranded or been cloned, or otherwise had code changes that would attempt to evade detection. (We&#8217;re not naming or linking to the apps given their malicious nature.) Commercial surveillance apps, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/22\/remove-android-spyware\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">like stalkerware or spouseware<\/a>, are typically surreptitiously installed by someone with physical access to a person\u2019s phone, often a spouse or domestic partner. These spyware apps silently and continually upload the contents of the person&#8217;s phone, including messages, photos, and real-time location data, and present a major security and privacy risk to the people whose phones are compromised.<\/p>\n<p>Play Protect intervened each time we tried to install spyware and stalkerware. The feature blocked the apps from installing, labeling the apps &#8220;harmful.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>We also picked a handful of predatory loan apps that were <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/04\/05\/google-personal-loan-apps-update\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">disguised as popular Android apps<\/a>. These loan apps upload the device&#8217;s contact list to a server under the guise of fraud prevention, and loan agents can use this access to send threatening and intimidating messages and calls to their contacts. The landing page of one of the predatory loan apps resembled a regular Google Play listing, but required the user to download and manually sideload the app from outside the app store.<\/p>\n<p>The Play Protect update did not restrict five predatory loan apps from installing at the time of our testing.<\/p>\n<p>We also tried to install a couple of apps that appear to be fake versions of other popular apps listed on Google Play. The apps we tested are similarly named and feature near-identical designs and user experiences, but are clearly underdeveloped knock-offs. One of the fake apps imitated a popular game and the other masqueraded as a widely used VPN app.<\/p>\n<p>Play Protect allowed these two apps to be installed, though it&#8217;s unclear for what purpose the fake apps were initially developed.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;With this recent enhancement, we&#8217;re adding real-time scanning at the code-level to Google Play Protect to combat novel malicious apps, regardless of if the app was downloaded from Google Play or elsewhere,&#8221; said Google spokesperson Scott Westover in an email to TechCrunch when reached for comment. &#8220;These capabilities will continue to evolve and improve over time, as Google Play Protect collects and analyzes new types of threats facing the Android ecosystem.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Sideloading allows the freedom to install any Android app but not without risk. Faced with an ongoing deluge of apps that quickly change their appearance and code, Google&#8217;s new real-time app scanning feature is an important last line of defense for billions of users and bound to only improve over time.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout embed-oembed embed--techcrunch\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"pQRq72Ugbh\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/30\/cybersecurity-101-android-security-how-to-protect-digital-privacy\/\">These Android features will help protect your digital privacy<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;These Android features will help protect your digital privacy&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/04\/30\/cybersecurity-101-android-security-how-to-protect-digital-privacy\/embed\/#?secret=X0x7L1dCFp#?secret=pQRq72Ugbh\" data-secret=\"pQRq72Ugbh\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Android&#8217;s in-built security engine Google Play Protect has a new feature that conducts a real-time analysis of an Android app&#8217;s code and blocks it from installing the app if it&#8217;s considered potentially harmful. Google announced in October the new real-time app scanning feature built into Google Play Protect that the company says can help catch ":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/05\/the-return-of-mega-rounds-in-fintech-and-where-all-the-former-mint-users-are-headed\/","title":{"rendered":"Why last week felt like 2021 in fintech"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><em>Welcome back to\u00a0<\/em><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/the-interchange\/\"><em>The Interchange<\/em><\/a><em>, where we take a look at the hottest fintech news of the previous week. If you want to receive The Interchange directly in your inbox every Sunday, head\u00a0<\/em><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/newsletters\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>here<\/em><\/a><em> to sign up! Last week, we chronicled some big rounds in the fintech space, Intuit&#8217;s decision to shutter Mint and what that means for startups and much more. Read on!<\/em><\/p>\n<h2>The return of mega-rounds<\/h2>\n<p>Last week felt like 2021. Well, sort of.<\/p>\n<p>There were at least three nine-figure funding rounds in the fintech space announced over the past week. It\u2019s rare enough these days to see ONE nine-figure round, much less two or three. So we were excited to say the least.<\/p>\n<p>First, I covered Brazilian banking-as-a-service startup <strong>QI Tech\u2019s <\/strong><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/31\/brazils-qi-tech-which-wants-to-decentralize-credit-away-from-banks-lands-200m-led-by-general-atlantic\/\">$200 million raise<\/a> led by General Atlantic. This was a big deal, besides just being a lot of cash, because it also marked the largest venture round in Brazil so far this year \u2014 not just in fintech, but across all industries. The company was gracious enough to share revenue figures, which is also not very common, noting that revenue was up 89% in the first half of 2023 compared to the same period last year. This also proves that infrastructure continues to be resilient, even during this downturn. Earlier this year, Visa announced it was going to acquire Brazilian payments infrastructure company Pismo in a $1 billion deal.<\/p>\n<p>Meanwhile, in the Middle East, <strong>Tabby<\/strong> nabbed <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/31\/buy-now-pay-later-platform-tabby-nabs-200m-in-series-d-funding-at-1-5b-valuation\/\">$200 million in a Series D funding round<\/a> that valued it at $1.5 billion. I was a bit surprised that a buy now, pay later platform would attract so much venture capital considering that so many players in the space have had their challenges in the past year or so. But TC\u2019s Tage broke it down for us, explaining that the markets in which Tabby operates don\u2019t have the same kind of access to credit cards that we do in the U.S. He wrote: \u201cAs a result, BNPL serves as a crucial source of credit; where it is seen as a convenience in developed markets with abundant credit options, it is essential for many consumers in the Middle East and, by extension, the Gulf.\u201d Tabby\u2019s profitable, too!<\/p>\n<p>And last but not least, Palo Alto, California\u2013based <strong>Next Insurance<\/strong> announced it had <a href=\"https:\/\/www.cnbc.com\/2023\/11\/01\/allstate-allianz-invest-265-million-in-next-insurance.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">landed $265 million in strategic capital<\/a> from Allianz and Allstate. As reported by CNBC, Next \u201cis nearing $1 billion in premium revenue but remains unprofitable.\u201d In April 2021, TechCrunch reported that the SMB-focused insurance provider had <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/01\/next-insurance-raises-250m-doubling-its-valuation-to-4b-in-under-a-year\/\">raised a $250 million round<\/a> at a valuation of $4 billion.<\/p>\n<p>Combined, the three fintech companies raised $650 million alone. And it\u2019s noteworthy that two of the three companies were located in markets outside of the U.S.<\/p>\n<p>While I don\u2019t think this means we\u2019re suddenly going to see mega-rounds on the regular, it\u2019s still encouraging news for the space!<\/p>\n<p>You can listen to Alex Wilhelm, Becca Szkutak and I (Mary Ann) drill down on the topic in Friday&#8217;s episode of Equity:<\/p>\n<p><iframe class=\"embed-iframe\" src=\"https:\/\/player.simplecast.com\/8714036e-1a70-4e44-8b79-1aeecedb2a53?dark=false\" width=\"100%\" height=\"200px\" frameborder=\"no\" scrolling=\"no\" seamless=\"\"><\/iframe><\/p>\n<h2>Where do all the Mint users go?<\/h2>\n<p>Now that Intuit says it is <a href=\"https:\/\/mint.intuit.com\/blog\/mint-app-news\/intuit-credit-karma-welcomes-minters\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">discontinuing<\/a> its personal finance app Mint in January, the company hopes most of Mint\u2019s customers will stay on and join Credit Karma. However, some Mint competitors told me they were already seeing a bump in new customers.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.monarchmoney.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Monarch Money<\/a>, a subscription-based money manager app, was one of them. You might remember that Mary Ann wrote about their <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/23\/monarch-raises-4-8m\/\">$4.8 million<\/a> seed round in 2021.<\/p>\n<p>The company shared via email that over the past week it saw \u201ctwice the number of users\u201d since the news broke. After the story went out, Monarch\u2019s execs got back to me to say that the normal sign-up rate jumped to 10x and ended the day at 20x higher.<\/p>\n<p>I later heard from a number of other Mint competitors, including Copilot co-founder Andr\u00e9s Ugarte, who told me that Nov. 2 was the company\u2019s \u201cbiggest day ever.\u201d Like Monarch, Copilot, who we covered <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/01\/16\/copilot-is-a-subscription-personal-finance-tracker-aiming-to-kill-mint\/\">here<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/21\/personal-finance-tracker-copilot-adds-support-for-apple-card-spreadsheet-imports\/\">here<\/a> in 2020, is a subscription-based personal finance tracker, and even from the first story, it was going after Mint.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe&#8217;re currently getting more than five times the number of users we see on a daily basis,\u201d Ugarte said via email.<\/p>\n<p>I covered <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/05\/23\/plenty-wealth-couples-fintech\/\">Plenty\u2019s pre-seed round<\/a> back in May, which provides a platform for couples to manage their finances together. Emily Luk, co-founder and CEO, said via email that the startup interviewed hundreds of millennial couples who manage their finances online, and found that of the 90% who had tried Mint, just 10% were still using it. Their reason? \u201cThe budgeting and reporting are too granular for this stage of their life, or it takes too much work to maintain,\u201d Luk said.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Mint was part of the last generation of products that helped people track and monitor their finances,\u201d Luk said. \u201cThe next generation will help people actively manage their money.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Plenty is still in waitlist mode; however, as a result of the news, the startup added a dropdown item on its waitlist to measure if new users signing up are looking to replace Mint. If so, those people will get early access and a way to import transaction history before Mint\u2019s January 1 cutoff.<\/p>\n<p>Meanwhile, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.useorigin.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Origin<\/a> had a well-timed launch on November 3. The startup claims it is \u201cthe first personal finance platform to provide holistic tracking of net worth, AI-powered financial guidance, automated investing, easy tax filing, estate planning and the option to meet with a Certified Financial Planner.\u201d It\u2019s too early to know if Mint\u2019s closing will affect user sign-ups, so hopefully I can come back with an update. \u2014 Christine<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout embed-oembed embed--techcrunch\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"y4jUWDjEvR\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/02\/personal-finance-monarch-intuit-mint\/\">Personal finance app Monarch sees bump in users following Intuit&#8217;s news it is closing Mint<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Personal finance app Monarch sees bump in users following Intuit&#8217;s news it is closing Mint&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/02\/personal-finance-monarch-intuit-mint\/embed\/#?secret=HN3iP6rhn0#?secret=y4jUWDjEvR\" data-secret=\"y4jUWDjEvR\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<h2>Weekly news<\/h2>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.revolut.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Revolut<\/a>, the fintech giant based in the U.K., has appointed a new CEO for its U.K. division. Francesca Carlesi will be in charge of Revolut\u2019s division in its home country, and Nik Storonsky remains the CEO of Revolut Ltd. It\u2019s worth noting that today\u2019s news comes as Revolut still doesn\u2019t have a banking license in the U.K. after years of back-and-forth with British regulators. The company applied for a U.K. banking license <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/11\/revolut-applies-for-uk-banking-license\/\">back in 2021<\/a>. More <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/02\/revolut-appoints-francesca-carlesi-as-new-uk-ceo\/\">here<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Unit, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/05\/17\/banking-as-a-service-startup-unit-closes-on-100m-at-a-1-2b-valuation\/\">which raised $100 million at a $1.2 billion valuation<\/a>, has launched a white label app, which it says allows software companies to embed banking and lending into their platform \u201cwith only one line of code.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Klarna employees were set to strike next week in the fintech\u2019s home country of Sweden, according to these <a href=\"http:\/\/tech.eu\/\" data-stringify-link=\"http:\/\/tech.eu\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">tech.eu<\/a><a href=\"https:\/\/tech.eu\/2023\/11\/01\/i-am-scared-of-what-is-going-to-happen-say-klarna-employees-ahead-of-expected-strike\/\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/tech.eu\/2023\/11\/01\/i-am-scared-of-what-is-going-to-happen-say-klarna-employees-ahead-of-expected-strike\/\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> articles<\/a>. But by the end of last week, the strike was called off. Via email, Klarna CEO and co-founder Sebastian Siemiatkowski told TechCrunch on Friday that \u201cafter an intense week of negotiations,\u201d the company had reached an agreement to join the Banks Employer Organisation by January 1, 2024. More\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/03\/fintech-klarna-reaches-agreement-with-workers-planned-strike-called-off\/\" data-stringify-link=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/03\/fintech-klarna-reaches-agreement-with-workers-planned-strike-called-off\/\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">here<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>As reported by Yahoo Finance, PayPal announced third-quarter earnings \u201cthat topped analyst estimates on both the top and bottom lines. The fintech company reported adjusted earnings of $1.30 compared to an estimate of $1.23. Revenue of $7.42 billion was slightly better than the expected $7.39 billion.\u201d The company&#8217;s shares \u201cclosed nearly 7% higher at $55.06 on Thursday as a strong full-year profit forecast also calmed market jitters about a spending slowdown,\u201d as reported by <a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/technology\/paypal-receives-sec-subpoena-tied-stablecoin-2023-11-02\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Reuters<\/a>. Interestingly, the company\u2019s new CEO, Alex Chriss, told <a href=\"https:\/\/www.americanbanker.com\/payments\/news\/paypal-ceo-companys-focus-has-not-been-clear\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">American Banker<\/a>: &#8220;Our cost base is too high and it is slowing us down. The company&#8217;s focus has not been clear.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Neon Money Club last week <a href=\"https:\/\/finance.yahoo.com\/news\/neon-money-club-first-black-143031116.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">became the first Black-owned tech company in the U.S.<\/a> to launch an American Express card: &#8220;According to information provided to AfroTech (and cited by Yahoo Finance), Neon Money Club \u2014 co-founded by Luke Bailey and Jackie Liao \u2014 has scored a partnership with American Express (Amex) &#8216;to launch a credit card that will challenge norms through its design and benefits, which include allowing users to invest reward points in the U.S. stock market.'&#8221; Hear more from Bailey in this article by TC\u2019s Dominic-Madori Davis <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/03\/black-founders-silicon-valley-bank-no-hard-feelings\/\">here<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Other items we are reading<\/strong>:<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.bizjournals.com\/washington\/news\/2023\/11\/02\/da-davidson-bank-mergers-acquisitions.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>Why this investment banker says bank M&amp;A is poised to rebound in 2024<\/em><\/a><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/sociable.co\/business\/digisure-launches-new-tool-to-prevent-fraud-on-sharing-platforms\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>DigiSure launches new tool to prevent fraud on sharing platforms<\/em><\/a><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.cnbc.com\/2023\/11\/02\/amazon-affirm-buy-now-pay-later-small-business.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>Amazon unveils buy now, pay later option from Affirm for small business owners<\/em><\/a><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.pymnts.com\/partnerships\/2023\/todaypay-teams-with-visa-bolster-refunds-as-a-service\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>TodayPay teams With Visa to bolster \u2018refunds as a service\u2019<\/em><\/a><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.fastcompany.com\/90977276\/daffy-fundraiser-tool-exclusive\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>Now you can start a fundraiser for any charity of your choice in seconds<\/em><\/a><\/p>\n<h2>Fundings and M&amp;A<\/h2>\n<p><em>As seen on TechCrunch<\/em><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/31\/charlie-which-provides-banking-services-to-seniors-secures-23-million-in-capital-six-months-after-launching\/\"><em>Charlie\u2019s senior-focused banking puts new funding toward stopping fraud<\/em><\/a> (The round came just six months after the company announced its seed round of funding, and launched. Since then, it has amassed \u201cthousands of users,\u201d according to its CEO.)<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/11\/02\/payroll-integrations-20m-employee-financial-wellness\/?mrfhud=true\"><em>Payroll Integrations grabs $20M to build employee financial wellness tools<\/em><\/a><\/p>\n<p><em>Seen elsewhere<\/em><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.ajc.com\/news\/business\/atlanta-insurance-technology-startup-raises-10-million\/HJNQ2SBFINC73ASDIOCHTKEXLI\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>Atlanta insurance technology startup raises $10M\u00a0<\/em><\/a><\/p>\n<p><a to revolutionise SaaS platforms with operational fintech features\u00a0<\/em><\/a><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.phocuswire.com\/kasa-living-series-c-funding\" target=\"_blank\" is launching two new subscription tiers, including a &#8216;Premium+&#8217; ad-free plan"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">X, formerly known as Twitter, is introducing <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/premium\/status\/1717977644996644948\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">two new tiers<\/a> for its subscription offering in order to bring in additional revenue. The social media giant is adding a new Premium+ tier that costs $16 per month and offers the &#8220;largest reply boost&#8221; and removes ads from the For You and Following feeds. The tier also comes with revenue-sharing, along with access to other creator tools.<\/p>\n<p>The second tier launching today is called &#8220;Basic&#8221; and costs $3 per month. The tier doesn&#8217;t come with a blue checkmark, but includes basic features like the ability to edit posts and post longer text and videos. It also offers a &#8220;small reply boost.&#8221;<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout embed-oembed embed--twitter\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">introducing Premium+<\/p>\n<p>\u2013 no ads in For You or Following<br \/>\u2013 largest boost for your replies (vs other Premium tiers or unverified users)<br \/>\u2013 access to our full suite of creator tools<\/p>\n<p>now available on Web \u270c\ufe0f <\/p>\n<p>subscribe here \u2192\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/Ywvyijo9CQ\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">https:\/\/t.co\/Ywvyijo9CQ<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&mdash; Premium (@premium) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/premium\/status\/1717977644996644948?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">October 27, 2023<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>Both of the new tiers are now available on the web.<\/p>\n<p>The new tiers join the standard X Premium tier, which replaced Twitter Blue. The tier costs $8 per month and gives users a blue checkmark, prioritized ranking in replies, bookmark folders, longer posts, text formatting, themes, sms two-factor authentication, encrypted DMs and more.<\/p>\n<p>The launch of the new tiers comes<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/06\/x-to-test-three-tiers-of-its-premium-service-ceo-says-code-shows-one-tier-may-be-ad-free\/\"> a few weeks<\/a> after <a href=\"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2023-10-05\/x-tells-bankers-that-advertisers-are-back-but-spending-less?sref=gni836kR\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bloomberg<\/a> reported that X was working on new subscription tiers.<\/p>\n<p>The introduction of the new tiers will give X additional ways to grow revenues as it deals with the loss in advertising dollars that it has faced since Elon Musk took the reins of the platform last fall. Musk&#8217;s controversial changes have turned away advertisers, as major companies ended up pulling their ads from the social network after their ads were displayed next to hate speech <a href=\"https:\/\/fortune.com\/2023\/08\/17\/twitter-x-ads-pro-nazi-account-right-wing-hate-groups\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-mrf-link=\"https:\/\/fortune.com\/2023\/08\/17\/twitter-x-ads-pro-nazi-account-right-wing-hate-groups\/\">and pro-Nazi content.<\/a> Earlier this month, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/technology\/us-ad-revenue-musks-x-declined-each-month-since-takeover-data-2023-10-04\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-mrf-link=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/technology\/us-ad-revenue-musks-x-declined-each-month-since-takeover-data-2023-10-04\/\">Reuters<\/a> reported that the company&#8217;s U.S. ad revenue has declined every month since Musk took over, with the latest figures showing a 60% year-over-year decline as of August.<\/p>\n<p>Since taking over the company last year, Musk has been looking for ways to generate additional revenue, and has gone so far as charging users in New Zealand and the Philippines <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/17\/x-starts-experimenting-with-a-1-per-year-fee-for-new-users\">$1 per year<\/a> in order to access the social network.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout embed-oembed embed--techcrunch\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"w3xp4u7QHX\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2023\/10\/27\/a-year-after-musks-takeover-x-says-an-average-user-spends-32-minutes-per-day-on-the-platform\/\">A year after Musk&#8217;s takeover, X says an average user spends 32 minutes per day on the platform<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute;
